The Third Manifestation: Tasawwuf within the Straight Path
Explaining the third reason for Ahl al-Sunnah's correctness and the third manifestation as tasawwuf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the trustworthiness of all Companions and explain why tasawwuf is considered a branch of Ahl al-Sunnah, not a separate path.

Core Idea
The straight path is moderate: avoiding extremes of sectarianism, anthropomorphism, and rationalism, with tasawwuf as a spiritual branch.

This lesson unpacks the third reason why Ahl al-Sunnah is the correct school: moderation between false extremes. The passage also introduces tasawwuf as the third manifestation of the straight path, showing that it is a legitimate spiritual discipline within Sunni Islam, not an independent path. You will learn how the Hanafi tradition situates itself against deviant groups and affirms tasawwuf within shari'ah bounds.

Guided Path
1
Identify the deviant groups and the Hanafi stance
The passage contrasts Ahl al-Sunnah with the Shi'ah (tashayyu') and the Rawafid. It states that Ahl al-Sunnah do not engage in takfir of any Companion. Locate the phrases describing these groups and their beliefs.
The term 'Rawafid' refers to those who reject the first three caliphs and declare takfir of Mu'awiyah.
2
Understand the extremes of tashbih and ta'til
Tashbih (anthropomorphism) likens Allah to creation; ta'til (deism/divine inactivity) claims Allah created intellects that run the universe. The Hanafi position is the middle path: affirm divine attributes without modality (bila kayf) and affirm Allah's sole control.
The 'ten intellects' refer to a philosophical emanation theory.
3
Recognize tasawwuf as the third manifestation
Shaykh Ahmad (the author of the matn) designates tasawwuf and suluk as the third manifestation of the straight path. It involves love of prophets and saints but must stay within shari'ah limits.
Tasawwuf is not separate from Ahl al-Sunnah; it is a branch.
4
Note the caveat: tasawwuf is a branch, not an independent path
The passage clarifies that tasawwuf is part of Ahl al-Sunnah's beliefs. The prayer 'Ihdina al-sirat al-mustaqim' in Surah al-Fatihah shows the path is one, with multiple manifestations.
This prevents the misconception that tasawwuf is a separate sect.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ت تشیع نہیں تاہم حضرت علی رضی اللہ عنہ اور ان کے متبعین کی تکفیر کی جاتی ہے اسی طرح روافض حضرت امیر معاویہ رضی اللہ عنہ (فاتح شام، کاتب وحی، ہادی [؟]مہدی[؟]) کی تکفیر کرتے ہیں خلفائے ثلاثہ رضی اللہ عنہ کی امامت وخلافت کے منکر ہیں اور حضرت علی سے دعوائے محبت میں بدتہ بین افراط کا شکار ہیں ۔ جبکہ اہل سنت کے چاروں ائمہ کا متفقہ عقیدہ ہے کہ تمام صحابہ رضوان اللہ علیہم اجمعین بشمول حضرت علی و معاویہ رضی اللہ عنہا عدول ہیں۔ معیار حق ہیں سب سے اللہ تعالی نے اپنی رضامندی کا قرآن میں سینکڑوں مرتبہ اعلان فرمایا ہے۔ تیسر ی وجہ مسلک حقہ عقیدہ تشبیہ اور تعطیل کے مقابلے میں معتدل ہے تشبیہ سے مراد اللہ تعالٰی کیلئے بھی انسانوں کی طرح ہاتھ چہرہ اور دیگر اعضاء ثابت کرنا اور معقیدہ تعطیل کا مبنی معقول عشرہ ہیں یہ فلاسفہ کا عقیدہ تھا جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ اللہ تعالی نے عقول عشرہ پیدا فرمائے ہیں اب تمام نظام کا ئنات یہی عقول چلا رہی ہیں اللہ تعالی (نعوذ باللہ ) معطل ہیں۔ ہمارا عقیدہ ہے کہ اللہ تعالٰی کیلئے یہ وجہ وغیرہ ہیں مگر انسانوں جیسے نہیں ہمارا کام ایمان لاتا ہے اور کیفیت اللہ تعالیٰ کو معلوم ہے اسی طرح ہم اللہ تعالی کو ہی مختار کل ، نظام عالم کا واحد تصرف مشکل کشا اور حانت روا، نفع نقصان کا مالک بلا شرکت غیرے بجھتے ہیں۔ مصداق ثالث کی وجہ شیخ احمد رحمہ اللہ ایک با کرامت صوفی بزرگ اور ولی اللہ تھے اس لئے انہوں نے تیسرا مصداق تصوف و سلوک کو قرار دیا ہے کیونکہ تصوف ایسی راہ ہے جس میں انبیاء اور اولیاء سے محبت وعقیدہ مسلمہ ہے مگر اس کی ایک حد مقرر ہے، محبت وعقیدت میں ایمانی حدود سے تجاوز نہیں کیا جاتا جس طرح کہ مجذو بین کا وطیرہ ہے یا پھر عشاق فساق کا۔ نیز یہ ماننے کی راہ ہے ہر کام حتی کہ احکام شرعیہ کو بھی منقل کی کسوٹی پر نہیں پر کھا جاتا کیونکہ عقل کل کے متبعین بالآخر لمحد وزندیق ہو کر اللہ تعالی کا بھی انکار کر بیٹھے ہیں ۔ نکته..... حقیقت میں تصوف و سلوک عقائد اہل سنت والجماعۃ ہی کا ایک شعبہ تے اگر اسے معدراق ثانی میں : کہ یہ کہا جائے کہ صراط مستقیم کے دو مصداق ہیں تو بے جانہ ہوگا۔ ..... هدانا الى الصراط المستقيم میں سورہ فاتحہ کی دعا لحد نا الصراط است تقسیم کی طرف تصحیح ہے
They are not Shi’ah, yet they declare takfir of Hadrat ‘Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) and his followers. Similarly, the Rawafid declare takfir of Hadrat Amir Mu‘awiyah (may Allah be pleased with him) (the conqueror of Syria, scribe of revelation, guide [Mahdi]), deny the imamate and caliphate of the three caliphs (may Allah be pleased with them), and suffer from excess in their claim of love for Hadrat ‘Ali. Whereas the agreed-upon belief of the four Imams of Ahl al-Sunnah is that all the Companions (may Allah be pleased with them all) including Hadrat ‘Ali and Mu‘awiyah (may Allah be pleased with them) are trustworthy. They are the standard of truth; Allah has announced His pleasure with them hundreds of times in the Qur’an. The third reason: The true school is moderate in the face of the beliefs of tashbih (anthropomorphism) and ta‘til (deism). Tashbih means affirming for Allah hands, face, and other organs like humans. The belief of ta‘til is based on the ten intellects; this was the belief of the philosophers, the gist of which is that Allah created ten intellects, and now these intellects run the entire universe, and Allah (we seek refuge) is inactive. Our belief is that for Allah there are these (attributes) such as hand etc., but not like those of humans. Our duty is to believe, and the modality is known to Allah. Similarly, we believe that Allah alone is the absolute controller, the sole disposer of the world system, the remover of difficulties, the provider, the owner of benefit and harm without any partner. The reason for the third manifestation: Shaykh Ahmad (may Allah have mercy on him) was a dignified Sufi saint and a friend of Allah; therefore, he made the third manifestation tasawwuf and suluk (spiritual wayfaring), because tasawwuf is a path that includes love and sincere belief in the prophets and saints, but it has a set limit; one must not transgress the boundaries of faith in love and devotion, as is the habit of the insane or the immoral lovers. Also, it is a path of following; every matter, even shari‘ah rulings, is not weighed on the scale of reason, because the followers of the absolute intellect eventually become atheists and heretics and deny Allah. A point: In reality, tasawwuf and suluk are just a branch of the beliefs of Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama‘ah. If it is considered a second manifestation, and it is said that the straight path has two manifestations, it would be inappropriate. ... 'Guide us to the straight path' in Surah al-Fatihah is a prayer; 'guide us to the straight path' is a directive for division, a correction.
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage is part of a commentary explaining the third reason why the Ahl al-Sunnah school is the correct one and the third manifestation of the straight path. The author first distinguishes Ahl al-Sunnah from the Shi‘ah and the Rawafid, emphasizing that Ahl al-Sunnah do not declare takfir of any Companion and consider all of them trustworthy. Then he explains that the true school is moderate between the extremes of tashbih (anthropomorphism) and ta‘til (deism). Tashbih is likening Allah to creation, while ta‘til is the philosophical belief that Allah created ten intellects that run the universe, leaving Allah inactive. The author affirms that Allah has attributes like hand and face, but not like humans, and that Allah is the sole controller. Then he introduces the third manifestation of the straight path: tasawwuf and suluk, as designated by Shaykh Ahmad (the author of the matn). Tasawwuf is a path of love for prophets and saints, but it must stay within the bounds of shari‘ah. It is a path of following revelation, not reason, because reliance on reason alone leads to atheism. The note clarifies that tasawwuf is a branch of Ahl al-Sunnah, not a separate path, and that if one were to say there are only two manifestations, that would be incorrect. The reference to 'Guide us to the straight path' in Surah al-Fatihah shows that the straight path is one, though it has multiple manifestations.

Key Terms
تشیع (tashayyu‘): The sect of Shi‘ah, particularly those who reject the first three caliphs and show excessive love for ‘Ali.
روافض (rawafid): A group of Shi‘ah who reject the caliphates of Abu Bakr, ‘Umar, and ‘Uthman and declare takfir of Mu‘awiyah.
تشبیہ (tashbih): The belief that Allah has a physical form similar to humans.
تعطیل (ta‘til): The belief that Allah is inactive and that the universe is run by created intellects.
تصوف (tasawwuf): Spiritual wayfaring involving love of prophets and saints, subject to shari‘ah limits.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the status of all Companions according to the four Imams of Ahl al-Sunnah?
A) They are all trustworthy.
B) Some are trustworthy, some not.
C) Only the first four caliphs are trustworthy.
D) They are not trustworthy.

Key Takeaway
The straight path is one, combining sound creed (avoiding tashbih and ta'til), respect for all Companions, and spiritual discipline (tasawwuf) within shari‘ah.

Definition of Iqtibas and Explanation of Khuluq ‘Azim
Definition of rhetorical device and explanation of indirect praise.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define iqtibas as a rhetorical device and explain why the author chose the description 'khuluq 'azim' without explicitly naming the Prophet.

Core Idea
The Prophet's character is the Quran; the description 'great character' alone suffices to identify him.

This lesson unpacks the opening lines of the text, where the author defines iqtibas and offers a salutation to the Prophet using only the epithet 'great character'. Through this, we see how rhetorical indirectness (kinayah) and the Prophet's unique virtue combine to make explicit naming unnecessary.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term iqtibas
Define iqtibas as a rhetorical device and note its function in scholarly writing.
Iqtibas is a form of indirect citation.
2
Locate the praise phrase
Find the phrase 'the one distinguished with great character' and observe that the Prophet's name is not used.
The phrase uses kinayah (indirect reference).
3
Recognize the objection
The commentator raises a natural question: why not name the Prophet explicitly?
The objection expects a response.
4
Analyze the answer
The description 'great character' is so uniquely associated with the Prophet that mention of it immediately brings him to mind.
This demonstrates the power of kinayah.
5
Examine the definition of 'khuluq ‘azim'
Define great character as a stable disposition enabling easy action, and note the strongest interpretation: the Prophet's character was the Quran.
This comes from the hadith of Aisha.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بیج سے مراد ہے کہ کلام کے اندر قرآن مجید کی کسی آیت یا حدیث نبوی یا کسی قصیدے یا شعر کی طرف اشارہ اس طور پر کرنا کہ اسے ذکر نہ کیا جائے ۔ والصلوة والسلام على من اختض بالخلق العظيم مخصوص کشیق عظیم ... اس سے کنا یہ حضور نبی کریم صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم مراد ہیں سے یا صلی مراد اشکال .... مصنف رحمہ اللہ نے حضور ا کرام صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے نام نامی اسم گرامی کی صراحت کیوں نہیں کی؟ جواب حضور اکرام صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کا خلق عظیم سے متصف ہو چاہتاج بیان نہیں اور یہ ایسی مریت ہے کہ جب بھی اس کا ذکر کیا جائے ذہن حضور ا کرام صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم ہی کی طرف منتقل ہو۔ تے لہذا کہنا یہ پراکتفاء فرمایا۔ تعریف خلق عظیم وہ ملکہ اور صلاحیت جس کی بناء پر بسہولت افعال انجام دیئے جاسکیں ۔ شور اکرم صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے لئے خلق عظیم شیخ احمد رحمہ اللہ نے اس میں تین اقوال نقل سکتے ہیں تاہم پہلا قول : وسرے اقوال سے قوی ہے۔ تقدیم اور دیگر قولوں کے ذکر اسیة التمر ابیض ہے یہ بات عیاں ہے۔ اقوال یہ ہیں: لاقوال حضرت عائشہ رضی اللہ عنہا سے جب حضور اکرم صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے اطلاق کے معمار سوال : کیا تو ارشاد فر مایا گیا کیا تم نے قرآن نہیں پڑھا؟ اس میں کیا شبہ ہے کہ قرآن مجید شور اکرم صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کی طبیعت بن چکی تمر ہے۔
The meaning of iqtibas is that in speech one refers to any verse of the Holy Qur’an or a prophetic hadith or any poem or poetry in such a way that it is not explicitly mentioned. And 'May blessings and peace be upon the one who was distinguished with the great character' — a specific great character... By this, it is alluded that the Prophet (peace and blessings of Allah be upon him) is meant. Objection: Why did the author (may Allah have mercy on him) not explicitly mention the noble name of the Prophet? Answer: The Prophet (peace and blessings of Allah be upon him) is characterized by great character, and the intention is not expressed, and it is such a virtue that whenever it is mentioned, the mind turns to him. Therefore, he sufficed with that. Definition of great character: It is the temperament and ability by which one can perform actions with ease. For the Prophet (peace and blessings of Allah be upon him), great character — Shaykh Ahmad (may Allah have mercy on him) transmitted three sayings in this regard, however the first saying is stronger than the other sayings. Prioritizing and mentioning other sayings, 'the example of the date is white' is obvious. The sayings are: The saying from Hadrat ‘Aishah (may Allah be pleased with her) when the Prophet (peace and blessings of Allah be upon him) was asked about the meaning of his character. Question: What was commanded? He said, 'Have you not read the Quran?' What doubt is there that the Quran became the nature of the Prophet (peace and blessings of Allah be upon him)?
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage defines iqtibas, a rhetorical device where one incorporates a Quranic verse, hadith, or poetic line without directly citing the source. Then it comments on the author's phrase 'may blessings and peace be upon the one distinguished with great character'. The commentator explains that the author deliberately avoided explicitly naming the Prophet to show that the description 'great character' is so uniquely associated with him that no explicit mention is needed. The question-answer format clarifies this. Then the passage defines 'khuluq ‘azim' (great character) as a stable disposition that facilitates action. It mentions three opinions on what constitutes the Prophet's great character, with the first being strongest: when asked about his character, the Prophet replied that he had adopted the Quran (i.e., his character was the Quran itself). The reference to 'the example of the date is white' may be an illustrative analogy but is unclear due to OCR.

Key Terms
اقتباس (iqtibas): A rhetorical device of alluding to a Quranic verse or hadith without explicit citation.
خلق عظیم (khuluq 'azim): The great character or disposition of the Prophet, enabling easy action, identified with the Quran.
کنا یہ (kinayah): An indirect reference or allusion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why did the author not explicitly mention the name of the Prophet in the praise?
A) The name was left out for brevity.
B) 'Great character' is so specific that the mind immediately turns to the Prophet.
C) The author considered it disrespectful.
D) The text was incomplete.

Key Takeaway
The great character of the Prophet is identified with the Quran, and indirect reference (kinayah) can be more eloquent than explicit naming when the attribute is unique.

Haqiqah, Majaz, Sarih, and Kinayah: The Four-Fold Classification of Word Usage
Defines the four categories of word usage and explains their enumeration with two Hanafi methods.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish haqiqah from majaz and sarih from kinayah, and explain the relationship between these two pairs in Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
Words in Islamic law are classified by literal vs. figurative use (haqiqah/majaz) and by clarity (sarih/kinayah), with sarih and kinayah applying to both literal and figurative.

In usul al-fiqh, understanding how words convey meaning is foundational. This lesson unpacks the third division of words as presented in Nur al-Anwar: the categories of haqiqah (literal), majaz (figurative), sarih (explicit), and kinayah (implicit). We will see how these two pairs interact and how Hanafi scholars have organized them in different ways.

Guided Path
1
Identify the usage dimension
First, determine whether the word is used in its original, lexically-assigned meaning or not. This is the primary split: haqiqah vs. majaz.
2
Classify as haqiqah or majaz
If the word is used in its original meaning, it is haqiqah; if used in a transferred or figurative sense due to a qarinah (contextual indicator), it is majaz.
3
Assess clarity of disclosure
Next, regardless of whether the word is haqiqah or majaz, check whether its intended meaning is immediately disclosed (sarih) or requires inference (kinayah).
4
Combine the two classifications
A word can be haqiqah-sarih, haqiqah-kinayah, majaz-sarih, or majaz-kinayah. This yields four categories. Note that sarih and kinayah are not exclusive to haqiqah.
5
Compare Hanafi methodological approaches
Al-Bazdawi separates the two pairs into different chapters (wujuh al-isti'mal for haqiqah/majaz, bab al-bayan for sarih/kinayah), while Sadr al-Shariah (in al-Tawdih) subsumes sarih/kinayah under haqiqah/majaz. The commentator prefers the latter.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله والثالث في وجوه استعمال ذلك النظم
تقسیم ثالث میں لفظ کا استعمال ملحوظ ہے کہ آیا لفظ اپنے معنی موضوع لہ میں استعمال، جو رہا ہے یا نہیں نیز اگر موضوع لہ میں مستعمل ہے تو کس حیثیت سے ہے؟ انکشاف معنی کے ساتھ ہے یا استار معنی کے ساتھ .
قوله : وهى اربعة ايضاً الحقيقة والمجاز والصريح والكناية ان چاروں اقسام میں وجہ حصر یہ بیان کی گئے ہے کہ دیکھا جائے گا کہ لفظ معنی موضوع لہ میں مستعمل ہے یا نہیں اگر اول ہے تو حقیقت ، ثانی ہے تو مجاز ہے پھر خواہ لفظ حقیقت ہو یا مجاز و حال سے خالی نہیں یا انکشاف معنی کے ساتھ استعمال ہوگا یا نہیں اگر اول ہے تو صریح اور ثانی ہے تو کنایہ ہے۔ نکته چونکہ صریح اور کنایہ کا تعلق حقیقت اور مجاز دونوں سے ہے اس لئے اصولیین نے یہاں دو طر یقے اور اپنائے ہیں
(۱) علامہ فخر الاسلام بز دوئی رحمہ اللہ کا اسلوب انہوں نے تقسیم ثالث کا عنوان دو جزوں پر مشتمل کر رکھا ہے: (القسم الثالث فی وجوہ استعمال ذالک النظم و جر یا نہ فی باب البیان ) حقیقت اور مجاز کا تعلق وجوہ استعمال سے اور صریح و کنایہ کا تعلق جریان فی باب البیان سے ہے۔ (۲) سام توضیح کا اسلوب انہوں نے تقسیم ثالث کی اولا دو قسمیں بتائی ہیں (۱) حقیقت اور (۲) مجاز ، پھر صریح اور کنایہ کو حقیقت و مجاز کی قسم قراردیا ہے ہی زیادہ بہتر ہے، جس طرح وجہ حصر سے واضح ہے۔
He said: The third [division] concerns the ways of using that expression. The third division considers the usage of the word: whether the word is used in its original meaning or not, and if it is used in its original meaning, in what capacity? Is it with disclosure of meaning or concealment of meaning? He said: And they are also four: al-haqiqah, al-majaz, al-sarih, and al-kinayah. The reason for enumerating these four types is that one looks at whether the word is used in its original meaning or not; if the first, it is haqiqah; if the second, it is majaz. Then, whether the word is haqiqah or majaz, it is not free from the situation: either it is used with disclosure of meaning or not; if the first, it is sarih; if the second, it is kinayah. Note: Since sarih and kinayah relate to both haqiqah and majaz, the usul scholars have adopted two methods here: (1) The method of Allamah Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi (may Allah have mercy on him): He made the title of the third division consist of two parts: (al-qism al-thalith fi wujuh isti'mal dhalik al-nazm wa jaryanihi fi bab al-bayan). Haqiqah and majaz relate to 'wujuh al-isti'mal', and sarih and kinayah relate to 'jaryan fi bab al-bayan'. (2) The method of the author of al-Tawdih: He first made two divisions for the third division: (1) haqiqah and (2) majaz, then he made sarih and kinayah subdivisions of haqiqah and majaz. This is better, as is clear from the explanation of the enumeration.
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage is from the commentary on Nur al-Anwar, explaining the third division of words (al-nazm) in usul al-fiqh. The author, following the matn, states that the third division examines how a word is used: whether it is used in its original meaning (haqiqah) or not (majaz), and then whether the meaning is disclosed (sarih) or concealed (kinayah). The classification yields four categories: haqiqah, majaz, sarih, and kinayah. The commentator clarifies that sarih and kinayah are not exclusive to haqiqah; they apply to both haqiqah and majaz. Two approaches by Hanafi scholars are noted: Imam al-Bazdawi separates 'wujuh al-isti'mal' (haqiqah/majaz) from 'bab al-bayan' (sarih/kinayah), while Sadr al-Shariah (in al-Tawdih) subsumes sarih and kinayah under haqiqah and majaz. The commentator prefers the latter as it aligns with the enumeration of four categories. This discussion is fundamental to understanding how words convey legal meanings in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
حقيقة (haqiqah): A word used in its original, literal meaning as per linguistic convention.
مجاز (majaz): A word used in a non-literal meaning due to a relationship (qarinah) preventing the original meaning.
صريح (sarih): A word whose meaning is disclosed explicitly, whether it is haqiqah or majaz.
كناية (kinayah): A word whose intended meaning is not apparent from the word itself but requires context or inference.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the basis for distinguishing haqiqah from majaz?
A) Whether the word is used with disclosure or concealment.
B) Whether the word is used in its original meaning or not.
C) Whether the word is used in a clear or ambiguous manner.
D) Whether the word is used in a general or specific sense.

Key Takeaway
Understanding the four-fold classification is essential for correct legal interpretation: haqiqah/majaz determine literal vs. figurative, sarih/kinayah determine evident vs. ambiguous, and both dimensions are independent.

The Four Methods of Inference from Text
Explains four ways a mujtahid can ascertain the intended meaning of a text

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four methods of inference from a legal text (ibarat, isharat, dalalat, iqtida') and distinguish which method is being used in a given scriptural argument.

Core Idea
A mujtahid infers rulings from texts through four ways: explicit wording, indication, implication, and necessary requirement.

In Hanafi usul, understanding how a ruling is derived from the Quran and Sunnah requires knowing the different ways a text conveys meaning. This lesson introduces the classical division into four methods: ibarat al-nass, isharat al-nass, dalalat al-nass, and iqtida' al-nass. You will learn to recognize each type and understand its role in istinbat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two broad categories
The commentator explains that inference is either from the wording (nazm) itself or from the meaning derived from it. Determine whether the ruling is taken directly from the words or from an underlying sense.
2
Distinguish 'ibarah from isharah
If the inference is from the wording and the wording was intended for that meaning explicitly, it is 'ibarah. If the wording was not intended for that meaning but still indicates it, it is isharah.
Example of 'ibarah: the verse 'Establish prayer' directly commands prayer. Example of isharah: the verse 'And of their wealth, take alms' indicates the imam cannot take zakat from his own wealth.
3
Distinguish dalalah from iqtida'
If the inference is from the meaning and it is a direct linguistic implication (e.g., a cause-effect relationship), it is dalalah. If it is a necessary assumption for the text to be valid or coherent, it is iqtida'.
Example of dalalah: 'Do not say to them 'uff'' implies prohibition of beating. Example of iqtida': 'The Prophet judged by...' requires he was alive.
4
Apply the distinctions to a new text
Given a verse or hadith, determine which method of inference would be used to derive a specific ruling. Check whether the ruling comes from the literal wording, an indirect indication, a logical implication, or a necessary assumption.
Use the classification diagram (from the commentary) to ensure no overlap.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : والرابع فى معرفة وجوه الوقوف على المراد تقسیم رابع ان طریقوں کے بیان میں ہے جن کے ذریعہ مجتہد و مستدل اعظم کی مراد سے واقف ہوتا ہے
قوله : وهى اربعة ايضاً الاستدلال بعبارة النص وباشارته وبدلالته وباقتضائه
وجه هر متدل کے استدلال کی دو ہی صورتیں ہیں یادہ اعظم سے استدلال کرے گا یا معنی سے اگر مستدل کا استدلال نظم سے ہو تو دیکھا جائے گا، اگر نظم اسی لئے چلایا گیا ہے " صراحتا نظم کی عبارت سے استدلال ہے تو یہ عبارت النص ہے، ورنہ اشارۃ النص ، اگر استدلال معنی سے ہوتو دو صورتیں ہیں: اگر یہ لغت کے اعتبار اسی نظم کا مفہوم ہے تو دلالت النص ، ورنہ اقتضاء النص ہے۔
قوله : وبعد معرفة هذه الاقسام قسم خامس يشمل الكل ماتن رحمہ اللہ فرماتے ہیں کہ نظم کی بنیادی طور پر تو یہی چار تقسیمات ہیں جن سے آگے چل کر کل میں قسمیں حاصل ہوتی ہیں سہل ضبط کے لئے خاکہ ملاحظہ فرمائیے
اصولیین کے ہاں مبحث فیہ بھی یہی اقسام ہیں۔ مگر ایک پانچویں تقسیم بھی بتائی گئی ہے۔ جس کا تعلق مذکورہ میں میں سے ہر قسم کے ساتھ ہے:
قوله : وهو اربعة ايضا معرفة مواضعها و معانيها وترتيبها واحكامها
He said: The fourth [division] concerns knowing the ways of arriving at the intended meaning. This fourth division explains the methods through which a mujtahid or one who seeks proof becomes aware of the intended meaning of the Text (the Lawgiver). He said: And they are also four: inference through the explicit wording of the text (ibarat al-nass), through its indication (isharat al-nass), through its implication (dalalat al-nass), and through its requirement (iqtida' al-nass). The explanation: Inference by the one seeking proof is of two types: either he infers from the Text itself or from the meaning. If the inference is from the wording, it is examined: if the wording was intended for that meaning explicitly, then it is ibarat al-nass; otherwise, isharat al-nass. If the inference is from the meaning, there are two forms: if it is a linguistic implication of that wording, then it is dalalat al-nass; otherwise, iqtida' al-nass. He said: After knowing these divisions, a fifth division encompasses all. The author (may Allah have mercy on him) says that basically these are the four divisions of wording, from which later all divisions are derived. For ease of memorization, see the diagram. Among usul scholars, these are the divisions in this topic. However, a fifth division is also mentioned, which relates to each of the aforementioned divisions. He said: It is also four: knowing their places, their meanings, their order, and their rulings.
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage explains the fourth division of words (al-nazm) in usul al-fiqh, which deals with how a mujtahid can infer the intended ruling from a legal text. The matn identifies four methods: (1) ibarat al-nass – the explicit wording of the text; (2) isharat al-nass – the indication of the text (a meaning implied by the wording but not directly stated); (3) dalalat al-nass – the implication of the text (a meaning that the wording necessitates linguistically); and (4) iqtida' al-nass – the requirement of the text (a meaning that must be assumed for the text to be meaningful or valid). The commentator elaborates that inference can be directly from the wording or from the meaning underlying the wording. If from wording and the wording was intended for that meaning, it is ibarah; if not directly intended but still derived, it is isharah. If from meaning and the meaning is a direct linguistic consequence, it is dalalah; otherwise, it is iqtida'. Then a fifth division is mentioned, which is a meta-classification encompassing all previous ones: knowing the places (where each type occurs), their meanings, their order, and their rulings – but this is not elaborated here. This classification is crucial for Hanafi usul as it systematically categorizes how scriptural evidence is used in legal reasoning.

Key Terms
عبارة النص ('ibarat al-nass): Inference from the explicit wording of the text that was intended directly.
إشارة النص (isharat al-nass): Inference from an indication in the wording that is not the primary intent but is understood from it.
دلالة النص (dalalat al-nass): Inference from the linguistic implication of the wording, such as a cause or condition implied.
اقتضاء النص (iqtida' al-nass): Inference from what the text necessarily requires for its validity or to avoid contradiction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which method of inference is used when the text's explicit wording is not intended but a meaning is derived from its indication?
A) 'Ibarat al-nass
B) Isharat al-nass
C) Dalalat al-nass
D) Iqtida' al-nass

Key Takeaway
The four methods of inference (ibarah, isharah, dalalah, iqtida') provide a comprehensive framework for deriving rulings from scriptural texts, each with distinct criteria based on wording or meaning.

The Meaning of Quru' in 'Iddah: Hayd vs Tuhr
Argument that قروء means الحيض, not الطهر, to preserve the count of three

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi rational argument (dalil aqli) that قروء means الحيض and critically evaluate the Shafi'i counterargument based on the lam in لعدتهن.

Core Idea
Hanafis prove that قروء means menstruation because counting purity periods would make the three either too many or too few.

In this passage, the author defends the Hanafi understanding of the Quranic term قروء (quru') by showing that the alternative interpretation (tuhr) leads to a logical contradiction with the number 'three'. This is a classic example of usul al-fiqh reasoning where meaning is derived by ensuring consistency with the text. We'll examine the argument and the inter-madhhab response.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed term
Locate the word 'قروء' in Quran 2:228 and note that its meaning is contested between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools.
The same word is used in the verse: وَالْمُطَلَّقَاتُ يَتَرَبَّصْنَ بِأَنفُسِهِنَّ ثَلَاثَةَ قُرُوءٍ
2
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that قروء means menstrual periods (الحيض). This is the position defended in the passage.
3
Analyze the Hanafi rational argument
Follow the logical demonstration: if قروء meant الطهر (purity periods), then counting three would lead to either excess (counting part of a tuhr) or deficiency (not counting the full tuhr of divorce). Both violate the precise number 'three'.
The argument is a dalil aqli (rational proof) based on the necessity of preserving the exact count.
4
Present the Shafi'i alternative and its proof
Imam al-Shafi'i argued that قروء means الطهر, and the lam in 'ليعدتهن' indicates time (i.e., divorce should be at the start of the 'iddah, during a purity period).
The Shafi'i proof is based on the linguistic function of the lam (لتعليل vs للوقت).
5
Evaluate the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is that the lam signifies purpose (تعليل), not time. The goal is to make the 'iddah easy by divorcing in a tuhr without intercourse, avoiding confusion about pregnancy.
Thus the Shafi'i linguistic proof is neutralized, and the rational proof for الحيض stands.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ہے
طہر مراد لیس تو یا زیادتی ہوئی یا کمی ہوگی اس لئے کہ جس طہر میں طلاق دی ہے اگر ہم اس کو شمار نہ کر میں تو زیادتی ہوگی کہ مین طہر مستقل اور طہر کا کچھ حصہ وہ ہے جس میں طلاق دی گئی اگر ہم اس طہر کو شمار کرنے میں تو ثلاثہ کے لفظ خاص پر عمل نہیں ہوگا کیونکہ ظاہر ہے کہ جس طہر میں طلاق دی ہے اس کا کچھ نہ کچھ حصہ گذر ہی گیا ہے دونوں صورتیں خرابیوں کو مستلزم ہیں اول کی صورت میں عورت پر عدت کو طویل کرنا لازم آتا ہے جبکہ دوسری صورت میں کتاب اللہ کے خاص ثلاثہ کے مقتضی پر عدم عمل لازم آتا ہے پس معلوم ہوا کہ قروء سے طہر مراد لینا درست نہیں ہے، اس لئے حیض مراد لیا جائے گا کیونکہ اگر قروء سے حیض مراد لیں تو ثلاثہ سے کم ہوگا نہ زیادہ۔ بعض لوگ کہتے ہیں کہ امام شافعی پر اعتراض کرنے کے لئے لفظ ثلاثہ کی ضرورت نہیں بلکہ یہ اعتراض تو لفظ قروء سے بھی ہو سکتا ہے اس لئے کہ ثلاثہ جمع کا لفظ ہے اور اقل جمع تین ہوتا ہے لیکن یہ بات صحیح نہیں ہے اور اس لئے کہ بعض اوقات جمع کا اطلاق تین سے کم پر بھی کیا جاتا ہے۔ جیسے الحج اشهر معلومات یہاں اشہر صیغہ جمع ہے حالانکہ حج کے مہینے تین نہیں بلکہ دو مہینے اور دس دن ہیں ۔
امام شافعی کو جواب امام شافعی کی دلیل کا جواب یہ ہے کہ ( لعد تھن ) میں لام وقت کیلئے نہیں بلکہ لام تعلیل کیلئے ہے۔ یعنی ان کو طلاق دو اس طریقے سے کہ ان کے لئے عدت کا گزارنا بآسانی ممکن ہو۔ اور یہ اس طرح ہوگا کہ ایسے طہر میں طلاق دی جائے کہ جس میں ولی نہ کی ہو کیونکہ اگر ایسے طہر میں طلاق دے کہ جس میں ولی کی ہے تو پتہ نہیں چلے گا کہ یہ حاملہ ہے یا نہیں اور اس کی عدت وضع حمل ہے یا تین قروء اور عدت کا شمار مشکل ہو جائے گا، اسی طرح حیض میں بھی۔
طلاق نہ دی جائے۔
If tuhr is meant, then either excess or deficiency occurs. Because if we do not count the tuhr in which divorce was given, there would be excess (three complete tuhrs plus part of the one in which divorce occurred). If we count that tuhr, then the specific word 'three' would not be fulfilled, since part of that tuhr has already passed. Both possibilities entail defects: in the first case the 'iddah is prolonged for the woman, in the second case the requirement of three (from the Book of Allah) is not acted upon. So it is established that taking quru' to mean tuhr is not correct; therefore it must mean hayd, because if quru' means hayd then there is neither less nor more than three. Some people say that to object to Imam Shafi'i, the word 'three' is not needed; the objection could be made from the word 'quru'' itself, because 'three' is a plural and the minimum of plural is three. But this is not correct, because sometimes plural is applied to less than three, as in 'al-Hajju ashhurun ma'lumat' (the months of Hajj are known) – here 'ashhur' is plural although the months of Hajj are not three but two months and ten days. The response to Imam Shafi'i's proof: The lam in 'li'iddatihinna' is not for time but for purpose, meaning: divorce them in such a way that it is easy for them to complete the 'iddah. That is, divorce them in a tuhr in which intercourse has not occurred, because if divorce occurs in a tuhr in which intercourse occurred, it will not be known whether she is pregnant or not, and whether her 'iddah is by delivery or by three quru', making it difficult. Similarly, do not divorce during menstruation.
Source pages p. 61

Commentary
This passage is a legal dispute (usul dispute) between the Hanafis and Shafi'is over the meaning of 'quru'' in the Quranic verse on 'iddah. The Hanafi position, as argued here, is that 'quru'' means menstrual periods (hayd), not purity periods (tuhr). The author presents a rational argument: if 'quru'' meant tuhr, counting the 'iddah would be problematic. If we exclude the tuhr in which divorce occurred, we would have three complete tuhrs plus a partial one, exceeding three; if we include it, the count would be incomplete because part of that tuhr had passed. Neither is acceptable. Therefore, only hayd works consistently. The author then addresses a potential objection: that the dispute relies on the word 'thalathah' (three), but some argue that the plurality of 'quru'' itself implies three. The author refutes this by noting that plural can refer to less than three, as in the Hajj months verse where 'ashhur' (plural) is used for two months and ten days. Finally, the author rebuts Imam Shafi'i's argument that the lam in 'li'iddatihinna' indicates time (i.e., divorce at the beginning of the 'iddah). Instead, it indicates purpose, meaning divorce in a way that makes the 'iddah easy, i.e., in a tuhr without intercourse, to avoid confusion about pregnancy.

Key Terms
قروء (quru'): Plural of قرء; in this context, Hanafis define as menstrual periods (حيض).
ثلاثة قروء (thalathatu quru'): Three 'iddah periods; the number three is specified in the Quran.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because الطهر is not a period of waiting
B) Because it would cause the 'iddah to be either more or less than three periods
C) Because the Quran explicitly says الحيض
D) Because Imam Shafi'i rejected that interpretation

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of قروء as menstrual periods (الحيض) is derived through rational reasoning (dalil aqli) to preserve the precise number three in the Quranic 'iddah ruling.

Definition of Amr and Its Specificity to Obligation (Wujub)
Defining amr and discussing its specificity to obligation via imperative form.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define amr according to Hanafi usul and explain why the imperative form is specific to obligation (wujub) rather than other meanings.

Core Idea
The imperative form (if'al) in Hanafi usul is exclusively specific to obligation, negating both commonality and synonymy.

This passage from the commentary on Noor al-Anwar defines the key usul term 'amr' and establishes its default legal significance. Understanding this definition is foundational because the Hanafi school builds its entire system of 'al-amr yufidu al-wujub' (the command indicates obligation) upon this precise linguistic specificity. The definition carefully distinguishes amr from other speech acts like requests and supplications, and the discussion of 'necessary' (lazim) clarifies the exclusive bond between the imperative form and obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition and its exclusions
Locate the definition: 'قول القائل لغيره على سبيل الاستعلاء افعل'. Note that 'قول' is the genus, 'على سبيل الاستعلاء' excludes requests/supplications (equality/humility), and 'افعل' excludes prohibitions (لا تفعل). Understand that 'فعل' here is the derived imperative form intending compulsion.
The condition that the speaker considers himself superior is essential.
2
Analyze the objection and Hanafi response
Read the objection that the restriction of superiority is problematic for grammarians and usul scholars. Understand the Hanafi response: the intended meaning is from usul scholars, and the superiority includes compulsion (luzum) of the action upon the addressee, absent in threat and enabling.
This refines the definition to exclude non-binding commands.
3
Understand the specificity: negation of commonality and synonymy
Examine the phrase 'ويختص... بصيغة لازمة'. The author intends to negate ishtirak (commonality) and taraduf (synonymy). Depending on grammatical parsing, the meaning is that the imperative form is specific only to obligation, and obligation is understood only from this form.
The concept of 'lazim' (necessary) is key: if coextensive, it negates both.
4
Note the conclusion: act is not obligatory for opponents
The text ends with 'حتى لا يكون الفعل موجبا خلافا لبعض اصحاب' – so that the act is not obligatory, contrary to some companions. This acknowledges a dissenting view, reinforcing that the Hanafi position is that the imperative form defaults to obligation.
The opponents likely hold that an imperative requires a qarina for obligation.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

هے كما قال الله تعالى اعملوا ما شئتم اور تجیز سے مراد عاجز کر دیتا ہے کقول تعالى فأتوا بسورة من مثل الخ

یہ بات تہدید اور تنجز میں نہیں پائی جاتی ہے۔
قوله : ويختص مراد . بصيغة لازمة
تشریح عبارت
یعنی وجوب صیغہ امر کیسا تھ خاص ہے۔ اور امر کا صیغہ وجوب کیسا تھ خاص ہے یہاں ے مصنف اشتراک اور ترادف کی نفی کرنا چاہتے ہیں کیونکہ یہاں پر (ہا) مختص پر داخل ہے اس صورت میں معنی یہ ہوگا صیغہ امر صرف وجوب کے ساتھ خاص ہے اس سے اشترک کی نفی ہو جا
ے گی۔
اور لازمہ کا مطلب یہ ہوگا کہ وجوب صیغہ امر کیسا تھ لازم ہے یعنی امر کی مراد جو کہ و جوب ہے وہ صیغے کے علاوہ کسی اور چیز سے سمجھ میں نہیں آتی تو یہ ترادف کی نفی ہو جائیگی یا (با) مختص به پر داخل ہے اس صورت میں معنی یہ ہوگا کہ وجوب صیغے کے علاوہ کسی اور چیز سے سمجھ میں نہیں آتا تو یہ تر ارف کی نفی ہو جائیگی پھر لا زمة سے مراد اگر لازم اعم ہو تو یہ بھی تراوف کی لفی ہوگی کیونکہ ملزوم تو لازم کے بغیر نہیں پایا جا سکتا ہے مگر لازم بغیر ملزوم کے پایا جاتا ہے تو اس صورت میں اشتراک کی نفی سمجھ میں نہیں آئیگی بہتر یہ ہے کہ لازم سے مراد لازم مساوی لیا جائے تو دونوں کی نفی ہو جائیگی۔
قولة : حتى لا يكون الفعل موجبا خلافا لبعض اصحاب
Discussion of command (amr). (Text:) 'And from it is the command, and it is the saying of a person to another on the way of superiority: Do (af'al).' Connection to what was said. Among the specific types that are frequently used in Shariah, one type is amr. Now the author (matn) begins the discussion of amr. Definition of amr: The saying of a person to another on the way of superiority: 'Do.' In this definition, (saying) is the genus including all words. By the restriction 'on the way of superiority', requests (iltimas) and supplications (du'a) are excluded. And by the restriction 'af'al' (do), 'la taf'al' (do not do) is excluded because it contains 'do not'. By 'f'l' (act) is meant the word that is derived from the present tense in the known manner, with the condition that it intends to make the action necessary, and secondly that the speaker considers himself superior. Objection: It is objected that if by this 'amr' the terminology of the Arab grammarians is meant, then the restriction of superiority is not correct because according to them, request and supplication are included in amr, so there is no benefit in excluding them. And if by it is meant the principles of jurisprudence scholars, then [the objection is]... as Allah says: 'Do what you will' (41:40), and tamjiz (enabling) means making incapable, as His saying: 'Then bring a surah like it' (2:23). Response: We respond that by this the amr of the usul scholars is meant, but in it the purpose is not merely superiority, rather it is a superiority that also includes making the action necessary for the addressee, and this is not found in threat (tahdid) and enabling (tamjiz). (Text:) 'And it is specific... to a necessary form.' Explanation of phrase: That is, obligation (wujub) is specific to the imperative form (sigha amr). And the imperative form is specific to obligation. Here the author intends to negate commonality (ishtirak) and synonymy (taraduf) because here the pronoun (ha) enters upon 'specific'. In this case, the meaning becomes: the imperative form is specific only to obligation, thus negating commonality. And the meaning of 'necessary' (lazima) is that obligation is necessary for the imperative form, i.e., the meaning of amr which is obligation is not understood from anything other than the form, so this negates synonymy. Or if the 'ba' enters upon 'specific', then the meaning becomes: obligation is not understood except from the form, thus negating synonymy. Then if by 'necessary' is meant a broader necessary, then synonymy is negated because the necessary (lazim) cannot exist without the object (malzum), but the necessary can exist without the object, so in that case negation of commonality is not understood. It is better to take 'necessary' as coextensive necessary, so that both negations occur. (Text:) 'So that the act is not obligatory, contrary to some scholars.'
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This passage is a definition and explanation of the term 'amr' (command) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author begins by stating that one of the specific types frequently used in Shariah is 'amr', and then provides its definition: 'the saying of a person to another on the way of superiority: Do' (قول القائل لغيره على سبيل الاستعلاء افعل). This definition is analyzed: 'saying' (قول) is the genus including all words; the restriction 'on the way of superiority' (على سبيل الاستعلاء) excludes requests (التناس? actually التماس) and supplications (دعا) because they involve equality or humility, not superiority; and the word 'افعل' (imperative verb) excludes prohibitions like 'لا تفعل'. The word 'فعل' here means an action derived from the present tense in the known manner, intending to impose the action, and the speaker must consider himself superior. An objection is raised: if this definition is from the Arab grammarians, then the restriction of superiority is invalid because they include request and supplication in 'amr'. If it is from the usul scholars, then threat (تہدید) and enabling (تنجز/تمجیز) would be included. The response clarifies that the intended meaning is from usul scholars, and the superiority here includes compulsion (لزوم) of the action upon the addressee, which is absent in threat and enabling. Next, the author discusses the specificity of the imperative form (صیغہ امر) to obligation (وجوب). The phrase 'ويختص... بصيغة لازمة' is explained: the author wants to negate both commonality (اشتراک) and synonymy (ترادف). If the pronoun 'ها' enters upon 'مختص', the meaning is that the imperative form is specific to obligation, negating commonality. 'لازمہ' means obligation is necessary for the form, i.e., obligation is understood only from this form, negating synonymy. Alternatively, if 'با' is considered, the result is the same. The passage ends by noting that the act is not obligatory, contrary to some scholars (خلافا لبعض اصحاب), implying the Hanafi position that the imperative form indicates obligation unless there is a contextual indication (قرینہ) otherwise.

Key Terms
أمر (amr): قول القائل لغيره على سبيل الاستعلاء افعل — the saying of a person to another on the way of superiority: do.
صيغة الأمر (sigha al-amr): The imperative form (e.g., افعل, ليفعل) that is specific to obligation in Hanafi usul.
وجوب (wujub): Obligation — the default legal significance of the imperative form according to Hanafi usul.
اشتراک (ishtirak): Commonality — the imperative form being common to multiple meanings (obligation, recommendation, etc.). Negated in Hanafi usul.
ترادف (taraduf): Synonymy — the imperative form being synonymous with other expressions for obligation. Negated in Hanafi usul.
لازم (lazim): Necessary — here used to describe the relationship between obligation and the imperative form: obligation is necessary (lazim) for the form, meaning it is exclusively indicated by it. If lazim is coextensive (مساوی), it negates both ishtirak and taraduf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi definition of 'amr' in this passage, which of the following is excluded by the restriction 'على سبيل الاستعلاء' (on the way of superiority)?
A) Prohibition (نهی)
B) Request (التماس) and Supplication (دعا)
C) Obligation (وجوب)
D) The imperative form (صیغہ امر)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi imperative form (amr) is defined as a superior's command 'if'al' and is specific to obligation (wujub), negating commonality and synonymy.

The Command Form Does Not Imply Repetition
Stating the Hanafi ruling on amr and takrar with Shafi'i difference

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position that amr does not necessitate or imply repetition, and compare it with the Shafi'i view.

Core Idea
A command like 'pray' requires one act, not many — repetition needs separate evidence.

This passage states a foundational usul principle: the command form (amr) does not demand or even suggest repetition. The Hanafi school holds that a single compliance suffices unless additional textual evidence indicates repetition. The Shafi'i school has internal differences: some say amr necessitates repetition, others say it only implies repetition. Let us examine the Hanafi position and its practical impact.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
What is the contested question? Does the command form (amr) by itself require or imply that the commanded act must be performed more than once?
2
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that amr indicates a single occurrence (marra wahida) and neither necessitates nor implies repetition.
Example: 'Establish prayer' means pray once; the five daily prayers are derived from separate evidence.
3
Note the Shafi'i split
Some Shafi'i scholars argue that amr necessitates repetition; others say it does not necessitate but implies repetition. The Shafi'i proofs are not fully given in the text.
4
Recognize the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: If a command implies repetition, every command would need to be done repeatedly unless specified. Hanafi: additional evidence (e.g., timings for prayer) sets the number.
5
Conclude the Hanafi view
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) Hanafi position is that repetition is not inherent in the command; it requires an external qarinah (indicator).
This principle applies to all commands unless a specific dalil shows repetition is intended.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ولا يقتضي التكرار ولا يحتمله سواء كان معلقاً بشرط أو مخصو صابر صف أولم يكن
احناف کا لاجب ہمارے نزدیک امر یہ تمہار کا تقاضا رکھتا ہے کہ بلانیت اس سے تکرار مفہوم ہو اور نہ احتمال رکھتا ہے۔ کہ نیت اور ارادے کے بعد اس سے تکرار والا معنی سمجھا جائے لهذا صلوا کامعنی ہے ایک مرتبہ نماز پڑھو اسی طرح صوموا کا معنی ہے ایک مرتبہ روزہ رکھو۔
شوافع کا مذہب بعض شوافع اس بات کے قائل ہیں کہ امر تکرار کا تقاضا کرتا ہے اور بعض کہتے ہیں کہ ہر امر تو تکہ اس کا تقاضہ نہیں کرتا البتہ تکرار کا احتمال رکھتا ہے آئیے ان کے د
His statement: And it does not necessitate repetition nor does it imply it, whether it is conditioned by a condition, specified by an attribute, or not. The Hanafi answer: In our view, the command demands a single occurrence, and without intention it does not necessitate repetition, nor does it imply that after intention and will the meaning of repetition is understood. Therefore, 'pray' means pray once, and similarly 'fast' means fast once. The Shafi'i school: Some Shafi'is hold that the command necessitates repetition, and some say that every command does not necessitate repetition but it does imply repetition. Let us see their...

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the principle that the command form (amr) does not imply repetition (takrar). The author begins by quoting a statement from the matn: 'And it does not necessitate repetition nor does it imply it, whether conditional or specified or not.' The Hanafi position is that a single command is fulfilled by a single performance; repetition is not demanded, nor is it even implied. Examples: 'pray' (sallu) means perform prayer once, not repeatedly; 'fast' (sumu) means fast once. The Shafi'i position is presented as split: some say amr requires repetition, others say it does not require but implies it. The Hanafi view is that even implication is absent. The text cuts off before detailing the Shafi'i proofs.

Key Terms
التكرار (al-takrar): Repetition of the commanded act more than once.
الاقتضاء (al-iqtida'): Necessitation or demand inherent in the command.
الاحتمال (al-ihtimal): Implied possibility or bearing a meaning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The command form obligates a single act; repetition is not inherent but may be added by external evidence.

Amr and Repetition: Hanafi Position and Shafi'i Objections
Usul dispute on amr and repetition with Hanafi proofs and refutations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on amr and repetition, and evaluate the Shafi'i counterarguments using the distinction between muwjib and muhtamil.

Core Idea
A command inherently requires only one performance; repetition is never implied by the mere imperative.

This passage tackles a foundational usul question: does an imperative (amr) demand a single act or repeated acts? The Hanafi school takes a firm position that amr neither necessitates nor even probabilistically implies repetition. The Shafi'i school is divided, with some arguing for necessity and others for probability of repetition. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to interpret divine commands and assess the strength of textual proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position and its linguistic basis
Begin by stating the Hanafi view as given in the matn: amr does not demand repetition nor bear probability. Note the examples of 'sallu' and 'sumu' indicating a single act.
The principle is rooted in the Arabic language; a command is fulfilled by a single instance.
2
Identify the two Shafi'i groups and their proofs
Group 1 (necessity of repetition) cites the hadith of Aqra' bin Habis. Group 2 (probability of repetition) relies on the indefinite object in the imperative form (e.g., 'darban') and conditional/descriptive verses like 'ifa jannabtum fatahharu'.
Note that the Shafi'i proofs are based on textual indications, not explicit consensus.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response to each proof
For the hadith: the Hanafi say Hajj is understood as once in a lifetime; the hadith does not prove repetition. For the indefinite object: it only indicates generality if a qarinah (contextual clue) is present, which is absent here. For conditional amr: each occurrence of the condition triggers the ruling separately, but the original command does not imply repetition.
The Hanafi response consistently preserves the principle that amr indicates a single act.
4
Understand the key distinction: muwjib vs. muhtamil
The text explains that muwjib (necessitating) is established without intention (niyyah), while muhtamil (bearing probability) requires intention to specify the meaning. This distinction clarifies why amr is not muhtamil for repetition.
Hanafi usul classifies texts as qat'i or zanni; the imperative without qarinah is qat'i in its indication of one act.
5
Apply the dispute's practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
The practical difference: a single command (e.g., 'perform salat') in the Hanafi school obligates one performance; in the Shafi'i view, some may require performance multiple times until certainty of compliance is achieved.
This affects how obligations like Hajj, zakat, or repeated acts are derived from general commands.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
امر مقتضی تکرار یا محتمل لتکرار ہے یا نہیں؟ قوله: ولا يقتضي التكرار ولا يحتمله سواء كان معلقاً بشرط أو مخصوصاً بوصف أو لم يكن۔ احناف کا مذہب ہے کہ ہمارے نزدیک امر تکرار کا تقاضا نہیں رکھتا اور نہ احتمال رکھتا ہے۔ لهذا صلوا کا معنی ہے ایک مرتبہ نماز پڑھو اسی طرح صوموا کا معنی ہے ایک مرتبہ روزہ رکھو۔ شوافع کا مذہب: بعض شوافع اس بات کے قائل ہیں کہ امر تکرار کا تقاضا کرتا ہے اور بعض کہتے ہیں کہ امر تکرار کا تقاضا نہیں کرتا البتہ تکرار کا احتمال رکھتا ہے۔ جو لوگ کہتے ہیں کہ تکرار کا تقاضا کرتا ہے ان کی دلیل اقرع بن حابس رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہ کی حدیث ہے کہ وہ اہل لسان میں سے تھے اس کے باوجود انہوں نے حج کے حکم سے تکرار سمجھ لیا۔ جو لوگ کہتے ہیں کہ امر تکرار کا احتمال رکھتا ہے ان کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ صیغہ امر مثلاً اضرب ہے اطلب منك ضرباً اور ضربا نکرہ ہے اور نکرہ اگر چہ اثبات میں خاص ہوتا ہے لیکن عموم کا احتمال رکھتا ہے لہذا جب کوئی قرینہ ہو گا تو اس کو عموم پر عمل کیا جائیگا۔ دونوں جماعتوں کے درمیان وجہ فرق: موجب اور محتمل میں فرق یہ ہے کہ موجب بغیر نیت کے ثابت ہو جاتا ہے اور محتمل نیت کے ساتھ ثابت ہوتا ہے۔ شوافع کا خیال ہے کہ اگر امر معلق بشرط ہو یا مخصوص بوصف ہو تو وہ تکرار کا احتمال رکھتا ہے۔ شوافع کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اللہ تعالی نے فرمایا (وان كنتم جنباً فاطهروا) کہ جب جنابت کی شرط پائی جائیگی تو طہارت کا حکم پایا جائیگا اور (السارق والسارقة فا قطعوا أيد يهما ... الخ) جب سرقہ کا وصف پایا جائے گا تو قطع ید کاحکم بھی پایا جائے گا۔ لیکن ہمارے نزدیک امر خواه معلق بشرط ہو یا مخصوص بالوصف ہو بہر صورت امر تکرار کا احتمال نہیں رکھتا۔ شوافع کی دلیل کا جواب: ہم کہتے ہیں کہ جب بھی جنابت اور سرقہ کا وصف پایا جائے گا تو طہر و اور فاقطعوا کا حکم الگ متوجہ ہوگا۔ اعتراض: اعتراض ہوتا ہے کہ جب آپ کے نزدیک امر تکرار کا احتمال نہیں رکھتا تو مطلقی تمسک میں تین کی نیت کرنا کیسے صحیح ہو گیا۔
Does amr necessitate repetition or bear probability of repetition? His statement: And it does not necessitate repetition nor does it bear it, whether it is conditional upon a condition or specific with a description or not. The Hanafi madhhab is that according to us, amr does not demand repetition nor does it bear probability. Hence 'sallu' means pray one time, similarly 'sumu' means fast one time. The Shafi'i madhhab: Some Shafi'is are of the opinion that amr demands repetition, and some say that amr does not demand repetition but bears probability of repetition. Those who say it demands repetition, their proof is the hadith of Aqra' bin Habis (may Allah be pleased with him) that he was from the people of language, yet from the command of Hajj he understood repetition. Those who say that amr bears probability of repetition, their proof is that the imperative form, e.g., idrib, means 'I ask for beating from you', and darban is indefinite, and indefinite although in positive context it is specific, it bears probability of generality. So when there is a qarinah, it will be acted upon with generality. The difference between the two groups: the difference between muwjib and muhtamil is that muwjib is established without intention, and muhtamil is established with intention. The Shafi'is think that if amr is conditional upon a condition or specific with a description, then it bears probability of repetition. Their proof is that Allah said, 'And if you are in a state of janabah, then purify yourselves' – when the condition of janabah is found, the ruling of purification applies, and 'As for the thief, male and female, cut off their hands' – when the description of theft is found, the ruling of cutting the hand applies. But according to us, whether amr is conditional upon a condition or specific with a description, in any case amr does not bear probability of repetition. The response to the Shafi'i proof: we say that whenever the description of janabah and theft is found, the rulings of 'fatahharu' and 'faqta'u' apply separately (i.e., each time). Objection: It is objected that when according to you amr does not bear probability of repetition, then how is it correct to intend three in tammat al-tamassuk?
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage presents a major usul dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools on whether the imperative (amr) implies repetition (takrar). The Hanafi position, drawn from the matn, is that amr neither necessitates nor even probabilistically implies repetition; it mandates a single performance. To illustrate, the commands 'sallu' (pray) and 'sumu' (fast) indicate one prayer and one fast. The Shafi'i school is split: some argue that amr necessitates repetition (e.g., the hadith of Aqra' bin Habis who inferred repetition from the Hajj command), while others argue that amr bears only probability of repetition, relying on the indefinite nature of the object (e.g., 'darban' is indefinite and can be general when a qarinah is present). The text explains the difference between 'muwjib' (necessitating) and 'muhtamil' (bearing probability) – the former is established without n iyyah, the latter requires n iyyah. A sub-dispute arises regarding conditional or descriptive amr: Shafi'is say such amr (e.g., 'ifa jannabtum fatahharu' or 'al-sariqu wa al-sariqatu faqta'u aidiyahuma') probabilistically implies repetition each time the condition/description recurs. The Hanafi response is that each occurrence of the condition/description triggers the ruling separately, but the amr itself does not imply repetition; it is simply applied repeatedly as the cause recurs. The passage concludes with an objection: if amr does not bear probability of repetition, how is it valid to intend multiple acts (e.g., three talāqs) in one utterance? This objection remains unanswered in this excerpt.

Key Terms
امر (amr): A demand to perform an action from a higher authority, typically through the imperative form.
تکرار (takrar): Performing the commanded act more than once.
موجب (muwjib): That which necessitates something without need for intention (niyyah).
محتمل (muhtamil): That which bears probability and requires intention (niyyah) to establish a specific meaning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position presented in this passage, what is the status of amr with regard to repetition?
A) Amr necessitates repetition unless specified otherwise.
B) Amr bears probability of repetition, requiring Niyyah.
C) Amr neither necessitates repetition nor bears probability; it indicates a single performance.
D) Amr only bears probability of repetition when it is conditional upon a condition.

Key Takeaway
The imperative (amr) in the Hanafi school mandates a single performance; it does not necessitate or probabilistically imply repetition.

7 min
Command Does Not Imply Repetition (Amr لا یفید التکرار)
Explaining that repeated worship acts are due to causes, not command repetition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle that amr does not imply takrar, identify its rationale (causes), and compare it with the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
Command does not create repetition; the cause does.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi usul principle that a command (amr) does not necessitate repetition of the commanded act. Repetition occurs only when the cause (sabab) recurs. This understanding distinguishes Hanafi from Shafi'i methodology and has practical implications in issues like divorce delegation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core principle
The passage states that repeated worship acts are due to their causes, not the command. Recognize that this is a basic Hanafi usul tenet.
The command is a single directive; repetition is external.
2
Analyze the evidence (talil)
Examine the examples: prayer repeats because time recurs; fasting repeats because Ramadan recurs; Hajj is once because its cause (the Kaaba) is one. This demonstrates that repetition tracks the cause, not the command.
This is a form of qiyas: the illa is the recurring cause.
3
Understand the objection and response
The objection splits obligation and performance. The response: whenever the cause occurs, a new command arises, so obligation is renewed via cause, not by original command.
This preserves the principle that amr does not imply repetition.
4
Contrast with Shafi'i position
Al-Shafi'i holds that amr implies possibility of repetition. The example: 'divorce yourself' intending two divorces – Shafi'i allows two. This contrasts with Hanafi where only one is given.
The difference arises from the linguistic interpretation of amr.
5
Apply to new scenarios
Given a command once, the Hanafi principle says the act is not repeated unless the cause recurs. Use this to derive rulings for other repeated obligations like zakat or expiation.
Always identify the cause behind the obligation.

They are. Whereas the obligation of worship is also based on the command of Allah Almighty. He said: 'And what is repeated of worship acts is due to their causes, not due to the command.' Answer: The answer is that worship acts are not binding due to the command, but rather they are repeated due to causes. Meaning: Time is the cause for the obligation of prayer, and Ramadan is the cause for the obligation of fasting. So whenever time and Ramadan are repeated, prayer and fasting will also be repeated. This is the reason Hajj is obligatory once a year, because its cause is the Sacred House of Allah, which is one. If it were due to repetition of command, then Hajj would also have to be repeated. Objection: An objection is raised: It is also possible that time is the cause for the obligation itself, and the command is the cause for the obligation of performance. Answer: The answer is that whenever the cause occurs, at that time a new command from Allah will be directed towards the servant. For example, whenever the time for prayer comes, a new command for prayer comes from Allah. Therefore, obligation also comes anew. Similarly, analogously. He said: 'And according to al-Shafi'i, since command implies possibility of repetition, a woman has the right to divorce herself twice if the husband intended that.' According to Imam Shafi'i, because command carries the possibility of repetition, if the husband intended two divorces in 'divorce yourself', then the wife will have the option to give herself two divorces.
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This passage discusses the usul principle that command (amr) does not imply repetition (takrar). The commentator explains a matn statement: repeated worship acts are caused by their causes (asbab), not by the command itself. For example, prayer is obligated at each time because time is the cause; fasting each Ramadan because the month is the cause. Hajj is obligatory only once because its cause (the Kaaba) is one. If command implied repetition, Hajj would be repeated. An objection suggests time may cause obligation and command cause performance. The response: whenever the cause (time) is present, a new command arises. Thus obligation is renewed. Then a Shafi'i example: if a husband says 'divorce yourself' intending two divorces, al-Shafi'i allows the wife to give herself two because he holds command implies repetition. This contrasts with the Hanafi view that command does not imply repetition.

Key Terms
امر (amr): A linguistic command that does not imply repetition; repetition is due to separate causes.
تکرار (takrar): Repeated occurrence of an act; not inherently from amr but from recurring causes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Because Hajj is a financial worship.

Key Takeaway
Command does not cause repetition; causes do.

The Cause of Qada' Obligation in Hanafi Usul
States the dispute on the sabab of qada'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the sabab of qada' and identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) of the dispute.

Core Idea
The cause of qada' is the same as the cause of ada'—the original command remains binding.

This lesson addresses a key usul question: what triggers the obligation to make up a missed act of worship? The matn concisely states the position of the verifying scholars (muhaqqiqun) that the cause (sabab) of qada' is identical to the cause of ada'. Some scholars dissent, but the Hanafi school relies on the principle that the original command remains effective until fulfilled.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
Read the source carefully. The muhaqqiqun hold that qada' is obligated by the same sabab as ada'. The phrase 'khilafan li'l-ba'd' indicates a minority opposing view. Determine what that opposing view might be.
The opposing view likely holds that qada' requires a new cause, such as a new command or the mere fact of missing the time.
2
Understand the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi argument is based on logical consistency: if the original command (amr) that made the act wajib remains in effect, it continues to demand fulfillment. No new cause is needed.
This relies on the usul maxim: 'Al-asl baqa' ma kana 'ala ma kana' (the original state remains as it was).
3
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
Consider a practical scenario: a person misses a voluntary fast that became wajib by vow. According to the muhaqqiqun, qada' is obligatory immediately because the original cause (the vow) still binds. The opposing view might delay obligation until a new cause (e.g., intention to make up) arises.
The difference affects whether qada' is an immediate duty or can be postponed.
4
Memorize the key maxim
The core principle for this lesson: 'Qada' is obligated by the same cause as ada'.' This is a foundational usul rule in Hanafi thought.
Commit this to memory; it appears often in furu' discussions about missed prayers and fasts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : والقضاء يجب بما يجب به الاداء عند المحققين خلافاً للبعض  قضاء کے سبب میں اختلاف: ان میں اختلاف ہے کہ قضاء کا سبب کیا ہے۔
He said: And qada' is obligatory by that by which ada' is obligatory, according to the verifying scholars (muhaqqiqun), contrary to some. Dispute regarding the cause of qada': They differ as to what the cause of qada' is.
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This passage presents a concise statement of a usul dispute. The matn states the position of the muhaqqiqun (verifying scholars) that the cause (sabab) which triggers the obligation of qada' (make-up) is the same cause that triggers the obligation of ada' (original performance), i.e., the original command (amr) that made the act wajib initially. However, some scholars hold a different view, possibly that qada' requires a new cause (like the volition or a new command). The passage does not elaborate further, but the student should understand that this is a recognized ikhtilaf within Hanafi usul. The muhaqqiqun are typically the leading Hanafi scholars such as Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad. The phrase 'khilafan li'l-ba'd' indicates there is a minority opinion.

Key Terms
سبب (sabab): The cause or ground that triggers an obligation
قضاء (qaḍā'): Make-up performance after the time has lapsed
اداء (adā'): Timely performance of an obligation

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) A new command from the Lawgiver.
B) The missed time itself.
C) The same cause by which ada' is obligated.
D) The intention of the individual.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi usul principle: the cause (sabab) of qada' is identical to the cause of ada'—the original command remains binding.

Types of Adaa in Rights of People: Complete, Deficient, and Resembling Qada
Explains three types of adaa with examples from huquq al-ibad

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the three types of adaa (kaamil, qaasir, mushabih bil-qadaa) in huquq al-ibad and apply the Hanafi principle that change of ownership can alter the legal ruling, using the hadith of Barīrah as evidence.

Core Idea
Performance (adaa) varies: complete, deficient, or hybrid—ownership change transforms legal status.

In Hanafi usul, the concept of adaa (performance) in the rights of people has three distinct categories: complete, deficient, and resembling qada. The passage illustrates each with practical examples from usurpation and marriage dower. Understanding these categories is essential for determining when an obligation is fully discharged and the legal effects of changes in ownership.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three types of adaa
List the categories: adaa kaamil (complete performance), adaa qaasir (deficient performance), and mushabih bil-qadaa (resembling qada).
These categories apply specifically to huquq al-ibad.
2
Analyze the example for each type
For each type, note the scenario and why it fits the category. For adaa kaamil: usurper returns item exactly as taken. For adaa qaasir: item returned with encumbrance. For mushabih bil-qadaa: slave given as mahr after purchase.
Consider what makes each example distinct.
3
Examine the hadith of Barīrah
Understand how change of ownership changes legal status. The Prophet ﷺ said 'For you it is charity, for us it is a gift.' This shows that the same object can have different rulings depending on ownership.
This analogy supports the mushabih bil-qadaa classification.
4
Determine the legal consequences
For the mushabih bil-qadaa example, note that if the husband frees the slave before delivery, it is valid; if the wife frees him, it is not. This is because ownership is still with the husband.
The dual nature of mushabih bil-qadaa creates specific rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ومنهار دعين المغصوب ورده مشغولاً بالجناية وامها وعبد غيره تسليمه بعد الشراء حتى تجبر على القبول وينفذ اعتاقه فيه دون اعتاقها
حقوق العباد میں اقسام اداء کی امثلہ
(۱) حقوق العباد میں ادائے کان کی مثال یہ ہے کہ غاصب منصوب چیز کو مالک کو اسی طریقے پر واپس کر دے جس حالت میں اس نے منصب کی تھی اسی طرح بائع عین مبیع کہ مشتری کے حوالے کر دیے۔ (۲) ادائے قاصر کی مثال یہ ہے کہ غاصب مخصو سب چیز کو جو اس حال میں واپس کرنے کہ وہ اس کے پاس مشغول بالجذایت یا مشغول بالدین ہوگئی ہو ۔ تو مناسب بری ہو جائیگا لیکن اگر مناصب نے اس کو دینی جنایت کے حوالے کر دیا تو غاصب سے قیمت لی جائینگی۔
(۳) مشابہ بالقضاء کی مثال یہ ہے کہ ایک آدمی نے دوسرے کے غلام کو اپنے نکاح میں مہر کے طور پر مقرر کر دیا۔ اور پھر وہ غلام خرید کر بیگم کے حوالے کر دیا تو یہ اس اعتبار سے تو ادا ہے کہ بعینہ اسی غلام کو بیگم کے حوالے کر دیاہے جس پر عقد نکاح ہوا تھا اور اس اعتبار سے مشابہ بالقضاء ہے کہ تبدل ملک سے تبدل میں لازم آتا ہے جیسا کہ حدیث بریرہ سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا ( لك صدقة ولنا هدية ) جس کا مفہوم یہ ہے کہ حضرت بریرہ کی ملکیت میں تو اس گوشت کی حیثیت صدقہ کی تھی لیکن جب اسکی ملک تبدیل ہوگئی اور حضوراکرم صلی اللہ علیہ کی طرف منتقل ہو گئی ۔ تو اس کی حیثیت تبدیل ہو کر صدقہ سے ہدیہ کی طرف منتقل ہو گئی۔ اسی طرح یہ غلام جب مالک کے پاس تھا تو گویا کہ یہ اور شخص ہے اور جب بیگم کے حوالے کیا تو اور بن گیا تو ادا ہونے کا تو ثمرہ یہ ہوگا کہ عورت کو اس کے قبول کرنے پر مجبور کیا جائیگا۔ اور مشابہ بالقضاء ہونے کا نتیجہ یہ ہوگا کہ عورت کے حوالے کرنے سے پہلے شوہر اس غلام کو آزاد کرے تو اس کا یہ فعل صحیح ہوگا اور اگر بیگم آزاد کرے تو صحیح نہیں ہو گا۔
His saying: 'And from them are the usurped item and returning it while it is occupied with a crime or its mother, and someone else's slave, delivering it after purchase so that she is forced to accept, and his manumission of it is effective but not her manumission.' Examples of types of performance in the rights of people: (1) An example of complete performance in the rights of people is that the usurper returns the usurped item to the owner in the same condition in which he usurped it, similarly the seller delivers the sold object to the buyer. (2) An example of deficient performance is that the usurper returns the usurped item while it has become occupied with a crime or debt at his place; then the usurper is absolved, but if the usurper handed it over for a crime, then the price is taken from him. (3) An example of resembling qada' is that a man designated another's slave as dower in his marriage, then purchased that slave and handed him over to his wife. So this is performance in that he handed over the very same slave that was the subject of the marriage contract, and it resembles qada' in that change of ownership entails a change in ruling, as is known from the hadith of Barīrah that the Prophet ﷺ said: 'For you it is charity, and for us it is a gift.' The meaning is that in Barīrah's ownership, that meat had the status of charity, but when her ownership changed and transferred to the Prophet ﷺ, its status changed from charity to gift. Similarly, when this slave was with the owner, he was one person, and when handed to the wife, he became another. So the effect of being performance is that the woman is forced to accept it, and the effect of resembling qada' is that if the husband frees this slave before handing over to the wife, his action is valid, but if the wife frees him, it is not valid.
Source pages p. 87

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the types of adaa (performance) in the context of huquq al-ibad (rights of people). The author begins by quoting a line from the matn which lists three scenarios: returning a usurped item, returning an item that has become encumbered, and the case of a slave given as mahr. Then he provides examples for each of the three types of adaa mentioned earlier: adaa kaamil (complete performance), adaa qaasir (deficient performance), and mushabih bil-qadaa (resembling qada). 

- For adaa kaamil: the usurper must return the item exactly as taken, or the seller delivers the sold item as agreed. This fulfills the obligation fully.
- For adaa qaasir: the usurper returns the item but it has been changed by a crime or debt. The usurper is discharged, but if the crime was committed by him, he pays its value. This performance is deficient because the owner receives something less than what was taken.
- For mushabih bil-qadaa: the example is a slave given as mahr by a man who then purchases and delivers him. The delivery is adaa because the specific slave is given, but it resembles qada because ownership changed (the slave became the man's property then the wife's), similar to the hadith of Barīrah where meat changed from charity to gift upon ownership transfer. The ruling: if the husband frees the slave before delivery, it is valid; if the wife frees him, it is not, because the husband's ownership transfers to her only upon delivery. This shows the dual nature.

Key Terms
اداء كامل (adaa kaamil): Performance that completely fulfills the obligation without any deficiency
اداء قاصر (adaa qaasir): Performance that is deficient in some aspect, yet the obligation is considered fulfilled
مشابہ بالقضاء (mushabih bil-qadaa): An act that has attributes of both adaa and qadaa due to change in the subject matter

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the example of mushabih bil-qadaa, if the husband frees the slave before handing him over to the wife, is the manumission valid?
A) Yes, because the husband still owns the slave before delivery.
B) No, because the slave is already considered the wife's property.
C) Yes, because the slave is a free person after manumission.
D) No, because the wife has the right to reject the mahr.

Key Takeaway
Performance in rights of people can be complete, deficient, or resemble qada when ownership change transforms the legal nature of the subject; the hadith of Barīrah establishes this principle.
