Fourth Division of Khabar: Types Based on Certainty
Expands on four types of khabar with rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify khabar wahid into four types based on certainty of truth/falsehood and apply the Hanafi ruling of 'wajib al-tawaqquf' to reports with equal probability.

Core Idea
A report's certainty determines its ruling: certain truth requires acceptance, certain falsehood rejection, and uncertain reports demand investigation.

In this passage, Mulla Jiwan expands upon the classification of khabar wahid into four categories according to the degree of certainty regarding its truthfulness. This division is crucial for a mufti to determine how to treat a report before issuing a ruling. We will explore each type, the proofs provided, and the specific ruling for reports that are neither certainly true nor certainly false.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the four-type classification
Mulla Jiwan states that khabar wahid has four types: 1) certain truth, 2) certain falsehood, 3) equal probability of truth and falsehood, 4) preponderant probability on one side. Identify the characteristics of each.
The fourth type is only mentioned and not fully elaborated due to the text ending abruptly.
2
Identify the proof for each type
For type 1: infallibility of prophets. For type 2: rational argument that humans are created and perishable, thus cannot be divine. For type 3: Quran 49:6 and the dual nature of a fasiq (Muslim yet sinful). For type 4: implied by the conditions of an 'adil narrator.
The proof for type 2 is purely rational (dalil aqli).
3
Understand the ruling for each type
Type 1: knowledge and action are obligatory. Type 2: rejection is obligatory. Type 3: wajib al-tawaqquf (obligatory pause and investigation). Type 4: not fully given in the text.
Mulla Jiwan relies on students' intelligence for the first two types, as they are obvious.
4
Analyze the concept of wajib al-tawaqquf
It means suspending judgment upon first hearing the report, neither accepting nor rejecting, until further evidence (qara'in) clarifies its truth status.
This is a key Hanafi principle in evaluating reports.
5
Note the incompleteness
The passage cuts off, leaving the fourth type's ruling and proof incomplete. Be aware that later sources may complete this.
This lesson focuses on what is available.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والتقسيم الرابع في بيان نفس الخبر
يہاں سے مؤلف رحمہ اللہ خبر واحد کی چوتھی تقسیم بیان کرتے ہوئے فرماتے ہیں کہ اس کی بھی چار قسمیں ہیں۔
قسم اول: ۔۔۔۔۔ وہ خبر جس کے سچا ہونے کا یقین ہو
مثال : حضور اکرم ا کی خبر اس پر دلیل یہ ہے کہ دوسرے انبیاء علیہم السلام کی طرح سردار انبیا ہ بھی کذب سمیت ہر قسم کے صغیرہ کبیرہ گناہوں سے معصوم ہیں
قسم ثانی: ۔۔۔۔۔ وہ خبر جس کے جھوٹا ہونے کا یقین ہو۔
مثال فرعون کا رب ہونے کا دعویٰ و قال انا ربکم الاعلی اس پر دلیل یہ ہے کہ فرعون ایک انسان تھا۔ اور تمام انسان حادث ہیں یعنی پہلے ان کا وجود نہیں تھا ۔ ھل اتى على الانسان حين من الدهر لم يكن شيا مذكوراً ) کیا انسان پر ایسا زمانہ نہیں آیا جب وہ کوئی قابل ذکر چیز نہیں تھا ) اور تمام انسان فانی ہیں کل مـن عـلـيـهـا فــان ويبقى وجه ربك ذو الجلال والاکرام (روئے زمین پر جو کچھ بھی ہے وہ سب فنا ہونے والا ہے اور صرف اللہ کی ذات باقی رہ جائے گی ۔ ) اور حادث وفانی معبود نہیں ہو سکتا۔
نکتہ:۔ یہاں حضرت مولنا شیخ احمد صدیقی المعروف ملا جیون رحمۃ اللہ علیہ نے دلیل عقلی سے استدلال کیا ہے اور صغری کے بعد نتیجہ نکالا ہے۔
قسم ثالث : ۔۔۔۔ وہ خبر ہے جس میں صدق اور کذب دونوں احتمال ہوں ۔
مثال :- فاسق آدمی کی خبر قال تعالى اذا جاءكم فاسق بنبأ فتبينوا (جب فاسق آدمی تمہارے پاس کوئی خبر لے کر آئے تو اسکی تحقیق کیا کرو )
خبر فاسق میں دونوں طرح کے احتمال ہونے پر دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس شخص کی دو حیثیتیں ہیں۔ ایک حیثیت یہ کہ یہ مسلمان ہے اور مسلمان کی خبر عموما سچی ہوتی ہے۔ دوسری حیثیت یہ ہے کہ یہ فاسق کا مرتکب ہے اور فاسق آدمی کی خبر جھوٹی ہوتی ہے ۔
نکتہ: ملا جیون رحمتہ اللہ نے پہلی دو قسموں کا حکم بیان نہیں کیا اور شاگردوں کی ذہانت پر انحصار کیا کیونکہ سب جانتے ہیں کہ جو خبر سچی ہوتی ہے اس پر علم اور عمل واجب ہو جاتا ہے اور جو خبر جھوٹی ہوتی ہے اس کا ترک واجب ہوتا ہے ۔ تیسری قسم کا حکم خود بیان کر دیا کہ یہ خبر ایسی ہے کہ اس پر توقف کیا جاۓ - حيث قال فهو واجب التوقف
واجب التوقف سے کیا مراد ہے: اس سے مراد یہ ہے کہ سنتے ہی ایسی خبر پر نہ صدق کا حکم لگایا جائے گا نہ کذب کا بلکہ خاموشی سے تحقیق کی جائے گی اور دوسرے قرائن و شواہد کی روشنی میں فیصلہ کیا جائے گا کہ یہ خبر سچی ہے یا جھوٹی
نکتہ: ۔۔۔۔۔ شواہد و قرائن کی تفصیل آپ اصول حدیث کی کتابوں میں پڑھ لیں گے۔
قسم رابع: وہ خبر جس میں صدق اور کذب دونوں احتمال ہوں ۔ لیکن ایک احتمال دوسرے احتمال سے راجح ہو۔
مثال : ۔۔۔ عادل شخص کی خبر ، جس میں روایت کی تمام شرائط موجود ہوں
نفس خبر کی تقسیم رابع بطریق وجہ حصر
And the fourth division concerning the report itself. From here, the author (may Allah have mercy on him) says, explaining the fourth division of khabar wahid, that it also has four types. First type: the report that is certain to be true. Example: the report of the Holy Prophet (peace be upon him). The proof for this is that like other prophets (upon them peace), the chief of prophets is also infallible from all major and minor sins, including lying. Second type: the report that is certain to be false. Example: Pharaoh's claim of being lord, 'He said: I am your lord, the most high.' The proof for this is that Pharaoh was a human being, and all humans are originated (i.e., they did not exist before). 'Has there come upon man a period of time when he was not a thing mentioned?' And all humans are perishable: 'Everyone upon it is perishable, and there remains the face of your Lord, the owner of majesty and honor.' And an originated and perishable being cannot be a deity. Point: Here, Maulana Sheikh Ahmad Siddiqi, known as Mulla Jiwan (may Allah have mercy on him), argued with a rational proof and drew a conclusion from the minor premise. Third type: the report in which both truth and falsehood are possible. Example: the report of a sinful (fasiq) person. Allah says: 'If a sinful person brings you news, then verify it.' The proof that the report of a fasiq has both possibilities is that this person has two aspects: one aspect is that he is a Muslim, and a Muslim's report is generally true; the second aspect is that he commits sin, and a sinful person's report is false. Point: Mulla Jiwan (may Allah have mercy on him) did not state the ruling for the first two types, relying on the intelligence of students, because everyone knows that a report that is true makes knowledge and action obligatory, and a report that is false makes its abandonment obligatory. He himself stated the ruling for the third type: that such a report must be paused upon. What is meant by 'wajib al-tawaqquf'? It means that upon hearing such a report, one should neither declare it true nor false, but silently investigate and decide in light of other indications and evidence whether the report is true or false. Point: You will study the details of indications and evidence in books of hadith principles. Fourth type: the report in which both truth and falsehood are possible, but one probability preponderates over the other. Example: the report of a just ('adil) person, in which all conditions of narration are present. The division of the report itself according to the method of enumeration.
Source pages p. 282

Commentary
This passage presents the fourth division of khabar (report) from the perspective of its own nature, as explained by the commentator Mulla Jiwan. The passage is a classification of reports into four types based on the degree of certainty regarding their truthfulness or falsehood. The author begins by stating that khabar wahid (single report) has four types. The first type is a report that is certain to be true, exemplified by the reports of the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him). The proof given is that prophets are infallible (ma'sum) from sins, including lying, so their reports are absolutely reliable. The second type is a report certain to be false, such as Pharaoh's claim of divinity. The proof is rational: humans are created and perishable, so they cannot be gods. The commentator notes that Mulla Jiwan used a rational argument (dalil 'aqli) here. The third type is a report where truth and falsehood are equally possible, such as the report of a fasiq (sinful person). The proof is from the Quran (49:6) and the reasoning that a fasiq has two contradictory aspects: being Muslim (implying truthfulness) and being sinful (implying falsehood). The ruling for this type is 'wajib al-tawaqquf' (obligatory pause), meaning one must suspend judgment and investigate further using other evidence. The fourth type is a report where one probability preponderates (rajih), such as the report of an 'adil (just) person who possesses all conditions of narration. The passage cuts off before completing the discussion of this type. The commentator emphasizes that for the first two types, the ruling is obvious (acceptance and rejection respectively), but for the third, investigation is required.

Key Terms
خبر (khabar): A report or narration that conveys information, specifically khabar wahid (single report) as the context is about divisions.
واجب التوقف (wajib al-tawaqquf): The ruling that one must pause and investigate a report before accepting or rejecting it, applicable to reports with equal probability of truth and falsehood.
فاسق (fasiq): A person who commits sin, whose report is considered unreliable and requires verification.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling (hukm) for the third type of khabar (report of a fasiq) according to Mulla Jiwan?
A) It must be accepted and acted upon.
B) It must be rejected and not considered.
C) It requires pause and investigation (wajib al-tawaqquf).
D) It is treated like the report of an 'adil person.

Key Takeaway
The fourth division of khabar wahid classifies reports by certainty, with the key ruling being that reports with equal probability of truth and falsehood require wajib al-tawaqquf (obligatory pause and investigation).

The Three Sides of Hadith Transmission: Sama', Hifz, and Ada'
Explaining the three sides of transmission and their subdivisions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three sides of hadith transmission and distinguish between the 'azimah and rukhsah modes for each side.

Core Idea
Hadith transmission has three sides—sama', hifz, ada'—each with a strict and a lenient mode, making six total methods.

The transmission of hadith is not a single act but a process with distinct stages. In this passage, the Hanafi usul text breaks down the process into three essential sides: hearing, memorizing, and delivering. Each side can be performed with full strictness ('azimah) or with permissible leniency (rukhsah), reflecting the fiqh approach to evaluating narrations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three sides
Read the definitions of sama', hifz, and ada' as given in the text. Understand that these are the three necessary stages for a complete transmission.
These sides correspond to: hearing from the teacher, memorizing what was heard, and conveying it to others.
2
Define each side precisely
For each side, note the specific action: sama' is first hearing from the narrator; hifz is memorizing from start to finish; ada' is delivering to fulfill responsibility.
The text emphasizes that hifz must be from beginning to end, showing the importance of complete retention.
3
Understand the bifurcation into 'azimah and rukhsah
Recognize that each side can be performed either with 'azimah (strict adherence) or rukhsah (allowable concession). This subdivision is a key fiqh tool.
In Hanafi thought, 'azimah is the norm; rukhsah is permitted under necessity (e.g., illness, lack of ability).
4
Enumerate the six resulting types
Combine each side with each mode to get six types: sama' bi 'azimah, sama' bi rukhsah, hifz bi 'azimah, etc. Confirm that the text explicitly lists these six.
This shows the granularity in evaluating a narrator's method.
5
Apply the classification to a scenario
Given a narrator's practice, determine which sides are present and whether they are performed with 'azimah or rukhsah.
This skill is used when assessing the reliability of a narration.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله ولهذا النوع المقصود ههنا

شرح قول ماتن و شارح:

ماتن مولانا ابوالبرکات عبداللہ سلی نے مختصر تعریف کے بعد فرمایا کہ نفس خبر کی تقسیم رابع کی یہی چوتھی قسم یہاں مقصود ہے اور اس کے تین اطراف ہیں۔ شارح رحمتہ اللہ نے ان اطراف ثلاثہ کو بیان کیا ہے۔

(۱) طرف سماع (۲) طرف حفظ (۳) طرف اداء

اطراف ثلاثہ کی تعریف

(1) طرف سماع: اس سے مراد سامع کا محدث سے اولاً حدیث کو سننا ہے۔

(۲) طرف حفظ: اس سے مراد یہ ہے کہ سامع نے محدث سے جو حدیث سنی تھی اسے شروع سے لے کر آخر تک حفظ (یاد) کرے۔

(۳) طرف اداء: اس سے مراد یہ ہے کہ جو حدیث سامع نے سن کر یاد کر لی تھی اسے دوسرے تک پہنچا دے تاکہ اس کی ذمہ داری پوری ہو جائے۔

پھر اقسام ثلاثہ میں سے ہر قسم میں دو پہلو (رخصت اور عزیمت) کے ہیں گویا تین کی بجائے چھ قسمیں ہو گئیں جو یہ ہیں:

(1) طرف سماع عزیمتاً (۲) طرف سماع رخصتاً (۳) طرف حفظ عزیمتاً (۴) طرف حفظ رخصتاً (۵) طرف اداء عزیمتاً (۶) طرف اداء رخصتاً
His statement: 'And this type is intended here.'

Explanation of the statement of the matn author and the commentator:

The matn author, our master Abu al-Barakat Abdullah, after a brief definition, said that this fourth type of the division of khabar is intended here, and it has three sides. The commentator (may Allah have mercy on him) explained these three sides.

(1) The side of hearing (sama'), (2) the side of memorization (hifz), (3) the side of delivery (ada').

Definition of the three sides:

(1) Side of hearing: It refers to the listener first hearing the hadith from the narrator (muhaddith).

(2) Side of memorization: It refers to the listener memorizing from beginning to end the hadith he heard from the narrator.

(3) Side of delivery: It refers to the listener conveying to others the hadith he heard and memorized, so that his responsibility is fulfilled.

Then, each of the three types has two aspects (rukhsah and 'azimah), so instead of three, there become six types, which are:

(1) Side of hearing with 'azimah, (2) Side of hearing with rukhsah, (3) Side of memorization with 'azimah, (4) Side of memorization with rukhsah, (5) Side of delivery with 'azimah, (6) Side of delivery with rukhsah.
Source pages p. 284

Commentary
Passage type: This passage continues the discussion of the fourth type of khabar, which is the one intended for transmission of hadith. It defines the three sides (atraf) of transmission: hearing (sama'), memorization (hifz), and delivery (ada'). Each side represents a stage in the process of narrating a hadith. The commentator then explains that each side can be performed in two ways: by 'azimah (strict compliance) or by rukhsah (permissible leniency). For example, hearing directly from the shaykh is the 'azimah, while hearing indirectly (e.g., through reading) might be a rukhsah under certain conditions. This subdivision into six categories shows the fiqh approach to hadith transmission, where the conditions of acceptance vary based on the manner of performance. The student should note that the Hanafi school is particular about these details, as they affect the reliability of the narration.

Key Terms
طرف سماع (taraf al-sama'): The aspect of hearing the hadith directly from the narrator.
طرف حفظ (taraf al-hifz): The aspect of memorizing the heard hadith.
طرف اداء (taraf al-ada'): The aspect of delivering the memorized hadith to others.
عزیمت ('azimah): The strict, full performance of the transmission duty without concession.
رخصت (rukhsah): A permissible leniency in the transmission method due to necessity or excuse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many total types result when each of the three sides of transmission is divided into 'azimah and rukhsah?
A) 3
B) 6
C) 9
D) 12

Key Takeaway
The three sides of hadith transmission—sama', hifz, and ada'—are each subdivided into 'azimah and rukhsah, yielding six distinct methods that Hanafi usul uses to evaluate the thoroughness of a transmission.
